It was decided (1) All local protection duties should be merged and handled by the township and town offices after their establishment in accordance with the county order. However, the responsibility for land and money should be urged by the Finance Bureau and the collection officials to urge each household together with the township and town heads and deputies. (2) The money owed before December 18th should still be collected by the former local protection official and the collection official to avoid compensation. (2) When will the township and town offices be established? It was decided that the township and town offices would be established on March 20th uniformly. (3) The county stipulated that the opening fee for township and town offices is 4 yuan per office. In addition to the advance payment for the seals and signs of 1 yuan each, should the remaining funds be issued to each township and town to handle the objects themselves, or should the district office handle them on their behalf? It was decided that the district office would handle items such as envelopes and strips, and the remainder would be returned. (4) How should we start to prepare for price stabilization? It was decided to handle it in accordance with the methods agreed upon by the Property Management Office. (5) There are still vacancies in the midwifery training center. It is proposed that the heads of each township and town send candidates for selection. It was decided that the heads and deputies of each township and town would guarantee the delivery by the deadline. (6) The Property Management Office allocated 100 yuan for burying floating coffins. How should it be distributed? It was decided to first bury them along the car roads in this area within the time limit to enhance the view. The township and town heads and deputies who are related will verify the allocation of funds for subsidies. If there is any surplus, it will be retained for future public cemeteries. (7) Omitted. (8) The head of Beiqiao Township proposed to merge the 29th map into other townships. Please decide on the proposal. It was decided to convene the relevant township heads on a regular basis to discuss it again. (9) Following the letter from the Construction Bureau, please direct the unfinished projects on each section of the Beihui County Road nearby. It was decided that the section chief would supervise the workers in each small section to be responsible for the project. (10) When will the land registration branch be established? It was decided that the land registration branch in this area would be established on March 15th to start registration, and the heads of each township and town should inform the owners to come to the office for registration within the time limit. The meeting adjourned after the discussion.

The All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association's Temporary Domestic Goods Market to Open 122

The All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association's temporary domestic goods market has been in preparation for many days. Yesterday, the tenth preparatory meeting was held, with 58 participating manufacturers. The opening ceremony is scheduled for 1:00 PM on the 8th. Resolutions were made regarding operating expenses, accommodation, and other matters. Many invitations have been sent to invite prominent figures from political, business, and academic circles to visit on that day. The association's declaration is recorded below: (Why are we launching this market? In short,)

We have two goals. First, it is to promote domestic goods. For every unit of domestic goods sold, one less unit of foreign goods will be bought. For every unit less of foreign goods bought, we reduce the outflow of Chinese money to foreign countries. These relationships are well known to everyone. Moreover, only by buying domestic goods can one appreciate their advantages and affordability. From then on, the word "domestic goods" will spread from one person to two, then to three, and be imprinted in everyone's minds. In this way, we will not fear foreign goods encroaching on the market for domestic goods. Our domestic goods factories will be easier to run. This is our first goal. The second is to provide relief to the disaster victims in Zhejiang. Because last year, Zhejiang Province suffered severe disasters. Taizhou need not be mentioned, but Huzhou, Shaoxing, and Ningbo also had many severely affected areas. We want to raise some funds for famine relief, so we came up with a method of selling "virtuous fruit tickets." On one hand, we are encouraging factories to donate goods, and we are using the donated goods as gifts for the virtuous fruit tickets. We want to take advantage of the launch of the domestic goods market to ask various manufacturers to donate some of their factory's products to help the numerous disaster victims in Zhejiang. This is our second goal. Because we have these two goals, this domestic goods market is being launched jointly by our All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association and five domestic goods organizations. Now, the venue for the market has been properly arranged (the Penglai Market in Xiaoximen, Nanshi). The opening date of the market has also been determined (March 8th). Fifty or sixty domestic goods manufacturers have joined the market and are preparing to open for business there. Come, come, come, everyone come! Citizens of Shanghai, everyone come and buy some domestic goods! Manufacturers of Shanghai, everyone come and promote some domestic goods, donate some domestic goods! Come, come, come, everyone come!)

The Ministry of Railways Investigates the Salary Robbery Case at the North Station 126

On the morning of the 1st of this month at 10:00 AM, the case of the theft of more than 5,970 yuan in salaries at the North Station of the two railway bureaus has been reported in the newspapers. It is reported that the Ministry of Railways believes that since there are many military police at the North Station, it is suspicious that public funds were stolen. Furthermore, the circumstances of the robbery at the time were quite suspicious. Why was it known to the thieves that the cashier of the relief office, Liu Tongfu, had received the salaries? After the thieves left, why did the railway police not bravely pursue them? Therefore, it is believed that the police chiefs of the two railway bureaus and the head of the police affairs section of the railway bureau should bear considerable responsibility. Therefore, it was decided to send personnel to Shanghai to thoroughly investigate the truth.

Also, Huang Renjie, the police chief of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway stationed at the South Station Police Office in the Shanghai-Jiading section, sent a letter yesterday to the Shanghai Special City Public Security Bureau, stating: "Regarding the matter of requesting assistance in apprehending [criminals], according to a telegram from Zhang Yunhui, a patrolman stationed at the North Station materials depot, on the morning of March 1st at around 10:00 AM, Liu Tongfu, the head of the dragon head office, took a tea room servant Shen Jiasheng on a pushcart to the Management Bureau's foreign relief office and received 5,880 yuan in salaries for the employees for February. They returned by pushcart. Just as they returned to the office in the dragon head room and were about to distribute the salaries, three short-clothed thieves, about 30 years old, speaking with a northern accent, each wearing blue cloth shirts and trousers, resembling workers, one with a shaved head and two wearing peaked caps, of medium height and strong build, suddenly rushed into the office, pulled out pistols, and intimidated everyone. They stole all 5,880 yuan of the February salaries and searched Liu Tongfu, the head of the office, taking a leather wallet containing more than 80 yuan in paper money. They forced him to open the safe. Because he was a little slow, a shot was fired, but fortunately, no one was injured. After the robbery, they escaped north towards Cao Mihang. Afterwards, workers Yin Maosheng and Shen Agou followed and chased after them and found more than 80 yuan in paper money in a ditch behind the coal platform. Please investigate and apprehend them. After investigation, the facts were confirmed. In addition to submitting a report for separate consultation and cooperation, it is appropriate to request that you investigate and find the stolen goods and thieves and bring them to justice."

The Two Married Daughters of the Sheng Family Also Sue for Division of Property 127

Guan Yi and Yi Bu Follow in the Footsteps of Their Younger Sisters

Request that the Estate be Divided into Nine Shares

The result of the Sheng family's dispute over property was a victory for the two unmarried daughters, Ai Yi and Fang Yi. Now, their two married elder daughters, Guan Yi and Chang Yi, are also following in the footsteps of their younger sisters and have filed a lawsuit against En Yi, Chong Yi, Sheng Yi, Yu Chang, and Yu You for division of property. The reason for their lawsuit is that when they married, they only received a small amount of dowry and did not receive any inheritance. They also learned of the 181st resolution of the Central Executive Committee, which interpreted that women inheriting property should have equal inheritance rights as men, regardless of whether they are married or unmarried. They are requesting that Sheng Xuanhuai's estate be divided into nine shares. Yesterday afternoon, the Provisional Court summoned [the defendants], but none of them arrived. However, Sheng Yuchang and Yu You engaged lawyers Jiang Yiping and others to appear on their behalf and requested a postponement. The plaintiff's lawyer opposed [the request], and after mutual arguments, the presiding judge adjourned the hearing for seven days.

The Fang Danchi Estate Lawsuit Was Heard Yesterday 128

Deng Guannan Falsely Accuses [The Plaintiff] of Restricting Freedom

Western Detective Appears in Court to Testify

Gold Leaves and Gold Pounds Were Not Given to the Concubine

The Coffin Shop Manager Will Be Called to Testify

After Fang Danchi retired from his position in Jiangxi Province, he lived in Shanghai until he died of illness on August 4th of the lunar calendar last year. All of his movable property, including bank deposits and goldware, had disappeared. His son, Da Can, believed that they had been stolen by his father's concubine, Deng, the concubine's father, Deng Guannan, and his father's friend, Wang Shutang, and servant Wang Dahan. Because he was in a hurry to return his father's coffin to his ancestral home in Huanggang, he did not resolve the matter legally at the time. Last year, the Deng father and daughter came to Shanghai from Wuhan, so Da Can went with Guannan to retain lawyer Zhan Jifeng to file a criminal complaint against Deng and others for joint theft in the Provisional Court. In the midst of issuing summonses, another incident occurred. Da Can still asked lawyer Zhan to continue to accuse the Deng father and daughter of falsely accusing him of kidnapping and damaging his reputation, while Deng also retained a lawyer to accuse Fang Da Can and his uncle Fang Fengchi of restricting her father Deng Guannan's freedom. After repeated summonses, out of consideration that Deng and others were living in Shanghai and had no way to find bail, it was ordered that lawyer Song Shixiang act as guarantor for Deng's parents, and lawyer Jiang Yiping act as guarantor for Wang Shutang, pending investigation. Yesterday afternoon, it was time for the continued hearing. Both sides came to court with their lawyers. At 4:00 PM, Judge Luo Renji finished hearing other cases from the Third Court and came to the Seventh Court to proceed with the hearing of the theft portion of this case. However, a certain Western detective from the Hongkou Police Station came to testify regarding Deng's false accusation, so he first ordered the Western detective to testify about the circumstances. According to him, after Deng made the report, he went to the Hongkou Grand Hotel to investigate and saw Deng Guannan, Fang Dacan, and a child in Room 19. The door of the room could be opened and closed at any time, and access was very free. Moreover, the room faced the road, and if Deng Guannan's freedom had indeed been restricted, he could have opened the glass window and shouted for help. He also submitted the police report of Deng's statement to the police station for inspection. Next, the plaintiff, Fang Da Can, stated that his father's deposits could be checked in the account book. When his father was ill, his uncles had asked about it, and his father initially did not expect to die from the illness, so he only told his uncles that there was an account to check. He did not know that the defendants had stolen the passbook and gold pounds and gold leaves after his father's death and destroyed the account books. Moreover, he did not know in what name the deposits were made or in which bank they were deposited, making it difficult to investigate. However, since the defendants had already admitted to the gold leaves and gold pounds, then the passbooks and other items were taken by them. Deng's statement that the gold leaves and gold pounds were given by her father was not true. Because his father and his uncles had not divided the property, the property belonged to everyone and would not be given away. He then submitted a distribution list and an account from Wang Shutang for inspection. His attorney, Zhan Jifeng, explained the reasons for submitting the two pieces of evidence, stating that the distribution list had Fang Danchi's own handwriting, which could be compared with the handwriting on the business card previously submitted by the plaintiff. He also proved that the words written on the back of the business card were indeed Danchi's handwriting. As for the account, it could also prove that the plaintiff's family had more than 3,000 yuan in early August of last year and did not need to use gold pounds as collateral to pay for the coffin. As for the 3,000 yuan, it was obtained by mortgaging tobacco leaf bills. Wang Shutang stated that the mortgage was made on August 12, which was also unbelievable. When questioned by Deng, she admitted that the checkbook had Danchi's own handwriting, but Wang Shutang said that the various payments were made on his behalf to repay debts. Judge Luo questioned, "Since the plaintiff's family needed funds for the funeral, they mortgaged the bill to urgently need the money. Then, they would not have the remaining money to repay old debts. Even if you wanted to repay the debts, the Fang family could take care of it themselves. Why would you repay them on their behalf?" Wang replied that there was a sum of 2,200 yuan that he guaranteed, so he repaid it on their behalf. Subsequently, the lawyer from the Ju Xiang Wood Company submitted two account books to prove that the coffin was purchased and paid for. He said that 36 gold pounds were initially used as a temporary deposit. On August 12, Wang brought cash to redeem the gold pounds. Lawyer Zhan immediately stated that according to Fang Fengchi's investigation with the wood company, there was no mention of gold pounds. If the company had any untruthful information, its manager could come to court to testify. Now, since he has not come, he should be ordered to come. Judge Luo immediately granted the request and waited for the summons to be served before the hearing continued. The account books were kept on file. The defendants Deng, Deng Guannan, and Wang Shutang were still guaranteed by lawyers Song and Jiang for bail.

The Local Court Heard the Counterfeit Banknote Case Yesterday 129

The Court Spent Three Days Inspecting [The Evidence]

A Total of 9,019 Counterfeit Banknotes Were Confiscated

The Judge Said the Defendants Had Done Great Harm

The Arguments Were Concluded Yesterday, Pending Sentencing

The Shanghai County Public Security Bureau cracked down on a counterfeit banknote manufacturing organization in the French Concession and detained six craftsmen who manufactured the counterfeit banknotes: Xu Yuting, Zhang Bingsheng, Zhu Yulin, Wang Jinshi, Chen Xiqing, and Wang Guoliang, who used the counterfeit banknotes. They were transferred to the Local Court, and after investigation, Wang Jinshi, Chen Xiqing, and others were also found to have committed opium offenses. Therefore, they were prosecuted with reference to Article 240, Paragraph 1, and Article 211 of the Criminal Law and the Anti-Smoking Law. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Shen Bingrong opened the court for hearing. According to the original detective Zhang Quanzhou, he saw Wang Guoliang holding a bunch of banknotes in front of Shouxian Lane. When he saw me, he quickly put the banknotes into his pocket, looking flustered. So, I followed him to his house, and the next morning, I arrested Wang Guoliang and found counterfeit banknotes in his galoshes on the spot. After taking him to the bureau, Wang confessed that the manufacturing organization was in the last house behind the cigarette company on Ximen Road in Ximen Lane. So, I immediately went to the address to arrest them. When I arrived, there was a mechanism on the door. When the bell rang, the lights inside went out immediately. So, we broke into the door and saw two engines and countless banknotes inside. The five people who were arrested were all wearing thin clothes and were working. A total of eight people were arrested, and three were released by the French Concession. When they were arrested, the main culprits, Chen Jinsheng and others, were smoking opium inside and later escaped. According to detective Wang Changlin, there were about four workers inside. According to detective Jiang Qiaosheng, when we went in, the order was already in chaos. There were four people in the engine room. According to the defendant Zhang Bingsheng, I am an apprentice doorkeeper. Xu Yuting said, I am a cook. The detective pointed out that he was arrested in the alley. The official said, after you finished cooking, your work was over, you must have helped with the manufacturing work. The official asked Zhu Yulin, are you working inside? Zhu claimed that the place was originally the Huaxin Art Company, and I am a proofreader. The judge asked whether you were proofreading the counterfeit banknotes. Moreover, you said at the company that you had a monthly salary of 30 yuan and a reward of 300 yuan. He replied, I did not say that. The official asked the detective, who is Zhu Jikun in the Public Security Bureau's records? He replied that he is a clerk. The director of the bureau himself reviewed the case. The official asked the defendant Chen Xiqing, and he replied that he was a typesetter, also denying it. The detective identified him as the one. Wang Jinshi said, I specialize in packing opium. Wang Guoliang said that he did not know Chen Jinsheng. His banknotes were given to him by a friend, Chen. The official asked whether Chen was Chen Jinsheng, and he replied, no. The judge said, this case is completely clear. How could you hire someone who is not a confidant as an accomplice and employ them? Moreover, your counterfeit banknotes are so real that only people in money houses can tell the difference. The court spent three days inspecting [the evidence] and confiscated a total of 9,019 banknotes, of which 415 were one-sided, and the rest were incomplete sets. You have done great harm. So, I asked prosecutor Lei to come to court and present his opinion, saying that the facts of the defendants' crimes in this case are already clear. However, the heaviest penalty for manufacturing counterfeit currency is life imprisonment, and the penalty for using counterfeit currency is also imprisonment for more than five years. I request that the presiding judge impose a heavy sentence. Wang Jinshi and others have also committed opium offenses, and I request that they be sentenced together. At this point, after defense lawyers Yan Yinwu and Ye Shengchao and others made their arguments separately, the judge announced that the arguments were concluded and that they would await sentencing. The defendants were remanded in custody.

The Zhifuli Lawsuit Reopened for Debate 132

The Hearing is Scheduled for 2:00 PM Today

The lawsuit between the Dalun Company and the Laodafang shop and other tenants in Zhifuli, Nanjing Road, regarding the surrender of the lease has been appealed to the Shanghai Provisional Court of Appeal. The court held a hearing on February 12 and announced that the arguments were concluded and that the verdict would be announced on February 24. Subsequently, due to the intense dispute between the two parties regarding the custom of surrendering indefinite leases in the Shanghai business community, the landlord believed that in an indefinite lease relationship, it is only necessary to give one month's notice, regardless of the reason, and both parties can terminate the contract at any time, and there is no opposite custom. Therefore, if the landlord wants to take back the property for reconstruction, he only needs to give notice on time, and the tenant cannot object. On the tenant's side, the reasons for termination are only three: (1) The tenant owes rent for more than three months; (2) the landlord takes back the property for his own use, but this does not apply to city houses or residences built specifically for rent, but only to spare rooms for rent; (3) the house is burned or rebuilt due to disrepair, but after the rebuilding, the original tenant has the right of first refusal to lease, and the rent can be negotiated. This is a custom that has been practiced in the business community for many years. The two parties have different opinions. The court ordered on the 24th that the verdict be temporarily suspended and that the custom be investigated by official authority before reopening the debate and rescheduling the verdict. It is reported that the case will be re-examined at 2:00 PM today. All circles in Shanghai are paying close attention to it. The Shanghai Chinese Ratepayers Association sent a public letter to the Court of Appeal, proving the custom of surrendering shop leases in Shanghai and requesting justice. The association's public letter is recorded below: "To whom it may concern, we received a letter from the Zhifuli Tenants Association on Nanjing Road, Fujian Road, stating that our members [omitted] are for both public and private convenience. Upon investigation, the statements in the letter are indeed facts. If this leasing custom is not confirmed and legal remedies are not provided, the impact will be incalculable. Based on the above, we hereby solemnly certify that the above-mentioned leasing custom is actually valid and request your court to provide legal remedies to maintain the social and economic order."

Case of Qu Chengqing Kidnapping: Continued Trial Yesterday 135

Awaiting Scheduled Sentencing

Qu Chengqing, a local employee of the Tiensheng Foreign Firm, was kidnapped on the night of January 11th from outside the back door of his residence at No. 1160 Haining Road. The Hongkew police rescued him from the bandit den at No. 1548 Shenteli, Seward Road, apprehended fourteen male and female bandits, and confiscated firearms. Previous reports detailed the matter and their interrogations at the Provisional Court. Yesterday afternoon, the trial continued. Except for Jiang Fuquan, Zhang Tingchen, and Gu Ronggui, who were found to be uninvolved and released, the remaining suspects, Wang Yuqing, Zhang Zhangji, Wang Afu, Xu Asan, Shen Adi, Guan Kangsong, Wang Qiwang, Chen Shizhong, He Qingen, as well as the wives, Lou Zhu's wife and Gu Yang's wife, were brought to court by the police. Qu Chengqing, represented by attorney Jiang Rong, testified that Zhang Zhangji and Wang Qineng were both holding guns when he was kidnapped and when he boarded the car. They guarded him during the journey. Upon arrival at the bandit den, Wang Yuqing ordered him to write two letters, both addressed to his family, but the ransom amount was not specified. Wang Afu, Shen Adi, Guan Liansong, and Wang Qineng all took turns guarding him at the bandit den. Xu Asan was a tea servant in the den and occasionally helped guard the hostage. There were two pistols in the bandit den, and the leader was Commander Li. He had not seen the other defendants, nor had he seen He Qingen, and had not heard that he was the leader. He also stated that he had not seen the handcuffs presented as evidence in the den. Chinese and foreign detectives stated that they apprehended Zhang Li's wife at He's house on Wuzhou Road based on Xu Asan's confession that He Qingen was the leader. Witnesses Feng Zhaoxiang and Lou A'gen successively testified that the handcuffs were used in a previous theatrical performance and were later lost. After the lawyers began their arguments, Judge Xu ordered Chen Shizhong to remain under bail of one hundred yuan, while the remaining men and women were returned to custody pending a scheduled sentencing.

On the evening of November 23rd last year, at 8:30 PM, several kidnappers suddenly arrived at No. 1958 North Chengdu Road and abducted Liu Shunan's six-year-old son, Si Yatou. Bandits Impersonate Officers to Search Lüzu Temple 137

Although Nothing Was Stolen

It Was Still a Robbery

On the afternoon of January 26th this year, at the Lüzu Temple near the Quanzhang Guild Hall on Longhua Road, west of Gaochang Temple, two men dressed in police uniforms, along with two other men and one woman, suddenly burst in. The woman claimed to be visiting the temple to burn incense, while the two men claimed to be from an official organization and came to search for contraband. They opened and searched the bedroom of the temple's incense keeper, Shi Kangfu, but found nothing. They then seized the temple's abbess, the nun Xin Cheng, and demanded that she quickly open the inner room for them to search. The nun realized that they were not good people, because the temple had been robbed in the past year, and she had been stabbed in the leg by the robbers. Therefore, she was always wary. Seeing their actions, she was terrified and broke free, running outside and shouting for help. Soldiers from the nearby military unit heard the alarm and immediately gathered a number of soldiers to rush to the scene. They caught the group as they were fleeing the temple and took them into custody. It was determined that the men in uniform were named Ding Debiao and Chen Qingyu, and the two men were named Lou Zhuan and Wu Axiang, and Wu Hu's wife. They were transferred to the district court prosecutor for questioning. Yesterday morning at 10:00 AM, Judge Deng, together with Prosecutor Yang, opened the first court to hear the case. The defendants were brought to the court. The victim, the nun Xin Cheng, testified that she was fifty-eight years old, from Shanghai, and was in charge of the Lüzu Temple. There were no visiting monks in the temple, only an old man named Shi Kangfu who was employed as an incense keeper. Around 4:00 PM on the 27th day of the twelfth lunar month last year, policemen suddenly arrived, saying they were searching for opium. But we don't smoke opium, so how could we have opium? At the time, they first opened the incense keeper's bedroom to search, and then he (referring to Lou Zhuan) grabbed me and forced me to open my bedroom. I refused. At that time, she (referring to Wu Hu's wife) interjected, telling me to quickly open the door and let them see. I was terrified and ran out to call for help. Fortunately, the soldiers arrived and took them into custody. Please investigate. The official asked how much was lost. She replied that nothing was stolen. She thought they had seen her run out to call for help, so they did not dare to stay and search. The defendant Lou Zhuan testified that he was from Hangzhou, currently unemployed, and staying at his friend Wu Shuangxiang's house. The remaining testimonies were evasive. Wu Axiang testified that he was formerly a rickshaw puller, but now he was unemployed at home because he was blind. This time, he accompanied his wife, Wu Hu, to the temple to burn incense, and there was no robbery. Wu Hu's testimony was the same as her husband's. Ding Debiao and Chen Qingyu both testified that they were patrolmen in a certain district station and went to the temple with Lou Zhuan and others to search for contraband, which was true, but they did not report it to their superiors. They begged for leniency. Prosecutor Yang rose to state that Lou Zhuan and the others were guilty of robbery and requested that they be sentenced according to the law. The special attorney Hu Yuanjun defended the defendants, requesting the court to sentence them according to the crime of fraud. The presiding judge declared the arguments closed and ordered the defendants to be remanded to custody to await sentencing. The victim was dismissed.

He arrived in Shanghai on the 11th day of the first month on a Nisshin Company steamer. After disembarking, he met a young trafficker of similar age who took him to his home and locked him upstairs. Then Chen Hua came to take him away today. After verifying the confessions, the head detective Cheng Yongnian transferred the case to the district court for trial yesterday.

Tuan Police in Pusong Town Fight Off Robbers 140

Bravely Pursue and Capture Three Robbers

The Tuan Police in Pusong Town (i.e., Beixinjing Town) in western Shanghai usually maintain strict security. Nearby villages also have defense teams to protect them, so there are rarely any robbery alarms in the area. The town's defense team suddenly received a report from a villager on the afternoon of the day before yesterday at 6:00 PM that a large boat was docked on the Wusong River behind Taobin, about two li west of the town. People with suspicious appearances were continuously boarding the boat. There were about thirty people, and it seemed that they were waiting for more accomplices. Please send a team to investigate as soon as possible. After receiving the report, the Tuan Deputy Commander Hou Jilan and the adjutant Zai Yuankui immediately ordered the squad leader Ren Xudong, along with the first team members Li Youji, Gong Guanming, Li Qiusheng, Gao Yangyuan, Gu Youde, Cai Honggao, and others, a total of more than twenty people, to rush to the scene. By the time they arrived, the members of the Zhangjiangdu sub-defense station of the first team had heard the alarm and arrived first, and they had already opened fire. When the main force arrived, the robbers were still putting up stubborn resistance with guns. The sound of gunfire was continuous for a time. Seeing that they were outnumbered, the bandits began to swim away in an attempt to escape. The members of each team bravely crossed the river and pursued them, and finally captured three bandits and one pirate ship. Only a ship donation certificate, No. 3505, and the name of the shipowner, Ji Jinghua, were found inside the ship. At the same time, officers from the Public Security Bureau's water patrol team also arrived one after another and apprehended four policemen. The rest escaped in the dark night. The team immediately took the captured bandits to the team headquarters. According to their confession, one was named Lu Jinyu, one was Tang Yujiang, and one was Zhou Rishun. They did not deny the identities of the captured and escaped accomplices. The bandits captured by the Public Security Bureau gave cunning confessions that could only be handled in conjunction with this case. Therefore, they specially sent Officer Li to the defense team for repeated consultations to inquire about the case. The team was focused on maintaining local tranquility, so they agreed to the request and immediately handed over the captured bandits to the Public Security Bureau for investigation. They also reported the course of events to their superiors. The captured pirate ship was taken by the water patrol team for investigation and verification.

Health Bureau Pays Attention to Horse Slaughter Inspections 141

Glanders-Infected Live Horses Confiscated for Rendering Oil

Public slaughter and sale of horse meat is permitted in all countries. However, horses that are slaughtered and sold that have glanders are an incurable disease. There is a possibility of mutual infection between humans and animals. Those that have already been discovered are easy to detect. But those that are hidden cannot be seen with the naked eye. Recently, the Municipal Health Bureau, in order to take precautions against citizens' meat hygiene, has ordered each slaughterhouse that from now on, whenever there is a live horse slaughtered and sold, it must be tested using an injection method. If a horse is found to have a glanders reaction, it will be confiscated for rendering oil. Each horse, regardless of size, will be given a subsidy of ten silver dollars to compensate the owner's loss.

An Unjust Death Under a Train 142

Old Man Dies Tragically Drunk

At 6:06 PM on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, the Shanghai-Songjiang Railway's 66th down train traveling from Shanghai to Songjiang was approaching the west shed door of the Wusongzhen train station. An old man was crossing the tracks from south to north on Tongji Road. The train driver saw him and immediately blew the whistle to warn him. However, the old man seemed to be deaf to the warning. By then, the train was already close, and the driver applied the brakes urgently, but it was too late. The old man was crushed in two at the waist by the train wheels, and his head was also crushed. The scene was too horrible to bear. Afterwards,

People proved that the deceased was Wang A'er, a sixty-three-year-old lacquer worker who lived in the Yao Huabang in northern Zhen. He was hard of hearing and had been drinking heavily at a tavern in the town before the accident and was staggering home. Unfortunately, he suffered this tragic accident. Afterwards, people reported to the deceased's family, and yesterday morning at 9:00 AM, they prepared a coffin for burial. The station staff also donated funds for condolences.

Leaving Her Husband for Her Lover 143

Hu Huang's Wife Has Another Love

Hu Jianming, forty-one years old, from Yancheng, Jiangbei, living in the Nanmatou area, makes a living pulling a rickshaw. His wife, Huang, thirty-one years old, was worried that her husband's labor income was difficult to bear and that household expenses were not always met. So she went to work as a female worker in a certain hosiery factory, so that she could use her monthly salary to subsidize the household. However, she was a middle-aged woman with remaining charm, and she disliked her husband for being old and unable to provide a rich income. She often felt depressed in her heart. Recently, she entered into an inextricable relationship with someone named A, and they hit it off, completely forgetting about her husband. Although Hu had learned of his wife's secret behavior, he did not argue with her because of his reputation. His wife became bolder and bolder. A few days ago, she left home without permission and did not return for several days. Hu was anxious about his wife's disappearance and searched everywhere for her, but to no avail. It was not until around 4:00 PM yesterday afternoon that she returned home. Hu questioned her sternly, asking where she had been staying for the past few days. Seeing that her husband was pressing her, she had no words to answer. Then, she became angry and retaliated, saying, "Am I not allowed to go out?" Hu was also furious and a big conflict arose between them. His wife took Hu to the first section of the first sub-bureau of the district and reported that she had disagreements with him (referring to Hu) and requested a divorce immediately. The director ordered a preliminary investigation and, because it was a matter of divorce, ordered him to prepare a document to be transferred to the Shanghai District Court for trial.

A Dead Body on a Rickshaw 144

The Rickshaw Puller Was Panicked

Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, east of Xinmin Road, Zhabei, there was a rickshaw with a concession license, carrying a man, about thirty years old, with a pale face, lying in the car. The rickshaw puller looked panicked and lingered on the road, looking worried. The police officer on duty there saw this and was suspicious, so he went forward to check. The man's body was as cold as ice, and he was dead. He questioned the rickshaw puller, who replied that he had been pulling the rickshaw on Beinicheng Bridge in the concession when someone asked him to take the man to the Jisheng Hospital in Zhabei for treatment. But before he could reach the hospital, the man had died on the way. I was carrying a dead person in my car, and I was panicked and didn't know where to go. I beg you to unload the corpse so that I can go back to work. I am very grateful. The officer on duty reported this to the Fourth District Headquarters, which ordered the local chief to report to the court for an inquest.

Three People Died on the Road 145

(1) Around 2:00 PM on the afternoon of the day before yesterday, an unnamed male corpse, about thirty years old, wearing a blue cloth cotton robe and a copper basin hat, was lying in Dunmuli, Manzhou Road, Zhabei. The local chief reported this to the Wuzhen Road Police Station in the Fourth District. It was later found that the male corpse was named Wang Azhen, thirty-one years old, residing at Chen Mingfa's house at No. 9 in the lane. He was sent to the hospital for treatment by his brother Wang Baosheng because he was ill. Unfortunately, he was too ill to be saved and was rejected by the hospital. He was supposed to be taken home by car, but he died halfway. The second landlord, Chen Mingfa, considered it unlucky to have a dead person in the house, so he did not allow the corpse to be carried into the house and had no choice but to abandon the corpse in the lane. Yesterday morning, the court sent someone to conduct an inquest, and it was confirmed that the death was due to illness. The corpse's family members were ordered to prepare a coffin for burial. (2) Jiang Yongsheng, forty years old, from Changshu, was previously a cook on the Xia Jiulang silk screen boat. Recently, he suffered from epilepsy and was dismissed by the shipowner. He went to Shanghai Hospital in the South of Shanghai for treatment, but never recovered. Recently, his finances ran out, so he slept on the streets at night. Yesterday morning at 8:00 AM, he was walking to the west of the Gongji Bamboo Shop on the Outer Ma Road when he suddenly fell to the ground due to an attack of his illness and died soon after. Zhou Lansheng, the local security chief, arrived at the scene to search. In his pocket, there was only a medical bill from Shanghai Hospital and nothing else of value. Since no family members could be found, he immediately reported to the yamen to receive a coffin for the inquest.

(3) Xu Desheng, forty-two years old, from Suzhou, an employee of the Dai Pig Rendering Oil Factory in Tanjia Bang, Wusong Outer Ma Road, left home around 8:00 AM yesterday morning to go to the factory to work. However, he suddenly fell to the ground at the intersection of Wenchang Road, talking nonsense. A few minutes later, he lost consciousness, foaming at the mouth. Passersby tried to send Xu to the hospital for treatment, but he only had a breath left. It is said that there is no hope of recovery.

Three Months Imprisonment for Bigamy 146

The woman Jin Yao, hired a lawyer in the Provisional Court to file a criminal complaint against her husband, Jin Guangfa, for bigamy, abandonment, and abuse. Because Jin failed to appear in response to the summons, the court issued a warrant to arrest Jin and the key witness Zhao Zhizun. Yesterday morning, Judge Sun Yuan continued the trial in the Second Criminal Court. The plaintiff, Jin Yao, stated that her husband, Jin Guangfa, used to work at the Tianyi Printing House. In July of last year, Jin became acquainted with a woman. A gangster found out and started blackmailing him, causing Jin not to go to the company for two days and his business to be suspended at this time. Later, I pleaded with the company to reinstate him, but all the salary was collected by me. Until one day, I learned that my husband and the mistress held a formal wedding ceremony at the Hongxiang Hotel on Xinzha Road. I rushed to the hotel at 3:30 PM, but they were already married. When I went to negotiate, my husband escaped through the back door, but I caught up with him and took him to the police station. The police chief ordered me to file a lawsuit with the court. That's why I filed the complaint. The defendant, Jin Guangfa, firmly denied bigamy. Judge Sun asked why the Hongxiang Hotel's book stated that it was a joyous event for the Jin family and had a wedding hall. Jin replied that it was also possible that someone with the same surname got married that day. Zhao Zhizun also denied being a matchmaker. Judge Sun verified the report and ordered the lawyers of both parties to argue.

The court sentenced Jin Guangfa to three months imprisonment for the crime of bigamy. The number of days of pre-trial detention was to be counted as two days for one day of imprisonment. The accompanying civil lawsuit dismissed Zhao Zhizun as innocent.

Truck Wheel Comes Off, Tram Traffic Obstructed 147

Yesterday afternoon at 5:30 PM, a cargo truck, city license No. 3662, was carrying more than forty barrels of tung oil from Yangshupu to the South Station to be transferred to Fuxing Transportation Company for transport to Hangzhou. When the truck reached Xiaoximen, it accidentally broke the steel pin on the rear wheel, and the right wheel fell off, causing the truck to fall onto the tram tracks. Fortunately, no one was injured. The trams traveling south from Ximen, such as the fourth, third, and second road trams, were all blocked. Later, the truck's workers tried to move the tung oil to the side of the road, and then used manpower to push the truck off the tram tracks. At the same time, a rescue machine was dispatched to tow the damaged cargo truck for repairs. The tram traffic was blocked for about half an hour before it resumed.

To the editor: I recently read an article in your newspaper's local news section on March 1 regarding the Qing Tian surveying ship clerk Li Mengzu drowning in the river. Some of the facts are incorrect. On that day, I went to the Hydrographic Survey Bureau on official business to discuss documents. Anxious to return to the ship, I hastily boarded a ferry, lost my footing, and fell into the water. Fortunately, I was rescued and there was no other reason. Fearing that distant rumors would be inaccurate, I am writing to request that your editor correct the record to reflect the facts. Sincerely, Li Mengzu

Society News

Urban Anecdotes: Lin 165

(4) In the Theater

Apart from movie theaters, there are about twelve or thirteen theaters in Shanghai that specialize in stage plays, including the Peking opera sections of various entertainment venues. Each theater has seating ranging from a few hundred to one or two thousand, so the number of audience members absorbed by various theaters each night is quite considerable when tallied up. The layout of Chinese old-style theaters has indeed improved compared to the past. There are many places that have been improved in terms of stage, background, seating, and decoration. Even teapots and towels seem to be much whiter, but the red and green colors in the eyes and the shouting and noise in the ears still maintain their original spirit.

The theater is a place of entertainment. The audience members certainly didn't run to the theater to deposit their bodies (temporarily) for a few hours because they had nowhere to put them. When we go to the theater to listen to a play, we at least want visual and auditory pleasure and physical and mental comfort. But in a big city like Shanghai, what are our impressions of general theaters? From the moment you enter the door until you leave the door, your eyes, ears, nose, throat, hands, feet, in short, your limbs and bodies, must be protected by the tense air around you.

We will not talk about the problem of reserved seats in the theater, because there are many problems that cannot be explained at once. Let's just talk about a spectator who wants physical and mental entertainment. What is the expression on his face in the theater? For example, if someone goes to the theater, when the usher sees him before he even steps in the door, he greets him as if he knows him and leads him in. However, he usually asks the guest first if he has a reserved seat or says ("Is this one ticket?"). The above is an exception if the guest has already reserved a seat.

After entering the venue, the guest will definitely choose a direction where he can hear clearly and see carefully. However, the result is ("Sir, I'm sorry, this place has already been reserved."). So the expression on the spectator's face is a little unnatural. If the theater is doing too well, then the expression on this spectator's face will be especially ugly. Sometimes the usher leads the guest around the venue to the east and to the west. The spectator's face is sometimes calm and sometimes tense, like a person walking with a bailiff in a temporary court. One can imagine what his face and heart are like.

Eventually, a seat is found. The usher has already taken great pains, but the guest is still very wronged. Especially if there are many people, there are always a few inevitable disputes. If the focus of the dispute involves ticket prices or money, then the rows of spectators who are not connected will be felt uncomfortable. Unless you reserve a box seat, which can be relatively comfortable, there are always some places in any hall or building that make people frown. The most annoying thing is that everyone is not acquainted, and at one point, inexplicably has to ("stand up to greet and send off."). For example, if there are sixteen seats in a row and five or six at both ends are already occupied, only four or five in the middle are left. If someone enters the seat, the people sitting at both ends will have to stand up to let him in. Letting in three people requires letting them in three times, which is not considered annoying. The most helpless thing is that if your noble neighbor gets up to pee, then you have to stand up twice in three minutes to send him off and greet him. As for whether your noble neighbor only has one bowel movement in a long period of four or five hours is another question.

Because when arranging seats in the theater, they are saving land like transplanting rice in a paddy field. The seats in each row are squeezed as much as possible. Not to mention fat people, who have to shout ("Excuse me") when going in and out. Even people with smaller statures dropping their hats or knocking over teapots is not a rare trick when going in and out. As for the rows of seats in front and behind, each seat is in a straight line with the one in front and behind it. If the audience members sit upright, then dozens of heads will become a vertical line. The audience members sitting downstairs often lean their shoulders and peek between the heads of the two people in front. However, the direction of the stage is far, and the location of the heads is near. The audience members behind look through the heads of the audience members in front, making it as difficult as looking at white clouds between two mountain peaks.

The colors and sounds in the theater are used to the extreme. The bright lights and the bright red and green colors shine on the eyes, often causing sleepiness. The sounds on the stage go without saying, are the price of the guests' money. The deafening gongs and drums are still echoing around the ears even after leaving the theater, but the source of the sounds offstage is difficult to explain. The most common are the cries of children, the coughing of gentlemen, the shouts of vendors selling candied haws, and the various sounds of teahouse waiters calling customers and the calls between them.

Move your gaze from watching the play to the walls, which are covered with many advertisements, almost like an enlarged newspaper. Especially for something like strong..., avoid..., menstrual..., plum..., tonic..., cough..., etc. The morbid state of the city is clearly performed on the walls, while the stage is still playing out a play from the fifteenth century. Once, a theater was playing ("New Changban Slope"). Mrs. Mi's arms holding Liu Adou was a Western doll, with fat white hands and feet, golden hair, and a pair of azure eyes. A child under the stage clapped and shouted "Western doll" non-stop. I don't know why, I had a thought, as if saying, "(Little Liu is of Slavic descent.)"

Interesting Story of a Female School Being Robbed Zhang Xiaoyan 166

Last Friday, on Yidingpan Road in western Shanghai, under the dim lights, a long-haired man, wearing a half-long, half-short coat, walked shivering. He looked around restlessly, as if afraid of being seen. After walking less than two hundred yards, he was met by a group of patrol officers. He was so frightened that he lowered his head and desperately walked forward. His panicked attitude proved that he had done something illegal and aroused the suspicion of the patrol officers, who shouted to stop him, ("Where are you running?").

("I...I...I'm going home."), he replied in a trembling voice.

"Are you wearing a serge robe? Is there a pattern?"

"No, it's satin, with flowers."

"How much money do you have in your purse?"

"I have tens of dollars."

"Hey, come here and look at the light... Oh, it turns out it's serge, where are the flowers... You're not a good thing, search him..." "Ahem, only twelve dollars. Where did this money come from?" Huge palms were sent to his face one after another.

"This...this was stolen from a certain female school," he replied, unable to bear the pain.

A group of patrol officers rushed to the certain female school and knocked on the door to investigate. It turned out that the male teacher's dormitory had been robbed. The window of Mr. Lu's room was half open.

"Hey, open the door, the detective wants to go in and investigate," they shouted like this.

"What's wrong in the middle of the night?" Someone in the room asked.

"I'm a detective, have you lost anything?"

"No, don't make noise, do you understand the rules? You can't knock on the door in the middle of the night."

"I was originally like this, what are the rules, I don't understand."

"I'll teach you now, you can't make noise in the middle of the night, that's the rule... Don't act like a teacher, I'll help you catch the thief, open the door quickly."

Mr. Lu had no choice but to get up and open the door. Under the light, he found that the leather suitcase placed on the bedside had been opened at some point. The newly purchased serge leather robe had disappeared without a trace.

Dongbao Reports on the Decline of the Chinese Flour Industry 168

Japanese Flour Industry is Very Optimistic

Page 20

According to Dongbao, Japan's flour exports to China are expected to suddenly flourish soon. Due to a shortage of funds, many Chinese flour mills have stopped operating, causing a sudden lack of flour supply in the Chinese market. Tianjin currently has 1.1 million bags in stock, Dalian has 1.8 million bags, and Shanghai has 600,000 bags, most of which are flour from Canada and other countries. Chinese-made flour is almost completely sold out. In the past two years, the situation of the Chinese flour industry has been poor, and several large factories in Shanghai are now shut down, resulting in an increasing shortage of goods. Japanese flour traders are therefore quite optimistic about trade with China and expect to receive a large number of orders soon.

Foreign Capital Encroachment on German Industry 171

Exceeds 1 Billion Marks

Two Million Unemployed

Berlin dispatch: Since the settlement of the reparations issue under the Young Plan in June of last year, Germany has repeatedly sought to rationalize its industries. However, due to a lack of funds, progress has been difficult. There have been many unemployed people during the winter. Last summer, there were about one million unemployed in the country. Late January statistics show that the figure has exceeded two million, setting an unprecedented record. Since the end of last year, capital from various countries has flowed in, especially American investment plans, which have been implemented one after another. The investments already decided by various countries include a loan of 500 million marks from Sweden, with the German government essentially granting the Swedish Match Company a monopoly on match sales for the next fifty years as collateral. Additionally, Germany's two major electrical companies, AEG and Siemens, have each borrowed 100 million marks and 30 million marks from the American General Electric Company. Furthermore, the world's only large chemical dye industry trust, I.G. Farben, has accepted Ford's huge investment. Opel Automobile Company is under the influence of American General Motors through investment. By this summer, investments from various countries will exceed 1 billion marks. Although there are signs of recovery in domestic industries due to the influx of capital from various countries, the encroachment of foreign capital and the monopoly of domestic industries by various countries have drawn criticism from informed individuals, but there is nothing they can do.

Phonographs Fall into Decline 172

▲ Drastic Decrease in Imports to the UK

Since the development of radio broadcasting, people in various European and American countries have been eagerly installing radios and listening to various types of music, which is extremely convenient. The once-popular phonograph has seen a sudden decrease in purchasers. Taking the UK as an example, according to statistics released by the Ministry of Commerce on phonograph imports to the UK over the past twenty years, the import volume in 1913 before the war was 25,000 units. Subsequently, it decreased year by year, and by 1928, it was less than 100 units. There was a slight increase last year (1929). The table is as follows:

1910: 18,802 units, £557,922

1928: 75 units, £58,800

1929: 1,415 units, £93,338

Rayon Not Suitable for Papermaking 173

Whether rayon can be used for papermaking is a question in the industrial world. According to recent experiments by the U.S. Bureau of Standards, it has been determined that it is not suitable for papermaking. This is because after rayon comes into contact with water, its fibers easily break and lack the toughness of rags and cotton. After forming a thin sheet, it cannot withstand the pressure and baking procedures, so it cannot be used for papermaking.

Mahjong Gambling Rampant in Japan 174

Tokyo dispatch: The Morals Section of the Tokyo Metropolitan Police Department's Security Bureau has found that there has been a large increase in mahjong clubs and mahjong research institutes in the city recently. It has been found that some of them are engaged in gambling and have women present. It is planned to draft a mahjong game control order based on the Games Control Ordinance to crack down on them.

Zheng He's Eunuch in Nanyang - YS 175

(7) Tua Pek Kong Bodhisattva

Among the soldiers and civilians who went to the South Seas with Zheng He's eunuch, there was a deputy leader named Wang Jinghong. Unfortunately, he died halfway. At this time, their ship was about to reach the South Seas.

After he died, he was naturally to be thrown into the sea (sea burial). However, his body floated up and down with the waves.

Three days later, the body was washed by the tide and finally washed into a crevice of rocks on a beach of a deserted island. Therefore, his body was silently exposed there for two days. However, his ghost finally found the local Malay chieftain in a dream.

(Hey, chieftain, bury my remains.) The ghost said to the Malay chieftain.

(Who are you? Where are your remains?) The Malay chieftain's dream soul replied.

(I am a Tang person. I came south with Lord Zheng He. I unfortunately died halfway, so they threw me into the sea for a sea burial. But I was washed here by the tide. My body has been wedged in the rock crevice on the beach and exposed for two days.)

(Oh, so that's the matter. But I can't agree to your request for me to do this, and I'm not happy to do such a dirty thing.)

(Ah, you're not happy and won't agree? I advise you to just do it and get it over with. Otherwise, in three days, the body will probably rot. At that time, your Malays might have an epidemic.)

(That doesn't matter, because you are a Tang person and we are Muslims who don't eat pork. Even if I don't bury your body, the Heavenly Emperor won't punish us. Besides, you are a Tang person who eats pork and rebelled against the Heavenly Emperor.)

(Alright, suit yourself. But I told you my good intentions, and you don't believe me, I can't make you believe me. Wait and see. Goodbye.) The ghost said, and disappeared.

When the chieftain woke up, he thought it was just a nightmare, so he didn't care about it.

Three days passed, and the deserted island began to have an epidemic. The Malay chieftain remembered his nightmare at this time. But many of his soldiers and civilians had already died. He couldn't think of any way to do it. He had no choice but to leave it to fate.

One day, it was June 30th, Zheng He's eunuch arrived at this deserted island in the South Seas. The Malay chieftain happily welcomed him because he wanted to get a method to avoid the epidemic from Zheng He's eunuch. He saw that none of the twenty or thirty thousand soldiers and civilians that Zheng He's eunuch brought were infected with this disease. So, he began to ask Zheng He's eunuch to give him guidance.

(You should bury his body.) Zheng He's eunuch only said this to him.

Later, the chieftain obeyed and did it. Sure enough, in two days, none of the natives on this deserted island were suffering from this disease. Since then, the natives of this deserted island have also built a temple for the deceased and offered incense to him. It is said that the deceased at that time was the Bodhisattva that the overseas Chinese in Nanyang now call (Tua Pek Kong). As for what place this deserted island is, it is said to be what is now the Dutch-owned Semarang.

Liang Xiongwan on America's Future Airfields 176

The New York Aeronautical Engineering Society has recently undertaken a great project. When this project is completed in the future, it will definitely make New York City even more noble and prosperous, and it can release a myriad of rays of light for New York's aviation industry. That is a great project, the greatest project in aviation history. Outside New York City, there are now countless low-lying grasslands, which cannot only be used for farming, but even animal husbandry is impossible. It is truly a barren land. The New York Aeronautical Engineering Society indeed has a brilliant idea. It will use this unproductive wetland to make an airfield. No matter how poor the place is, whether it is low or wet, regardless of what difficulties and inconveniences there are in terms of engineering, this wetland is suppressed and overcome by human power. This human power is like this: the river mud dug out from the bottom of the river is used to fill and raise this low-lying grassland.

The airfield mentioned above is the Secaucus Airfield, which is currently under construction. The site is a large open low-lying area in Jersey, New York, three and a half miles from downtown New York City. The airfield occupies more than a thousand acres of wetlands. It has now been thickened with river mud. The mud is dug out from the bottom of the Hackensack River. It will take about five million cubic yards of river mud. The river mud that has been dug out is 2.5 million cubic yards. It is said that 25,000 to 30,000 cubic yards of river mud can be dug out in 24 hours every day. The equipment of the airfield is also very impressive. The airfield is equipped with an aircraft showroom, offices, storage warehouses, a parking field, and a hotel for tourists to stay in. In the future, when this airfield is completed, New York's aviation industry will definitely advance even faster, needless to say.

Japan's Industry Over the Past Ten Years 177

▲ Highest Amount Reached in Showa 3

According to the Japanese Ministry of Commerce and Industry's survey of the growth and decline of Japanese industry, with a few exceptions, it increased by about five times compared with Taisho 3 and 8. In the following two years, due to the appropriate post-European War period, it gradually decreased, with the 10th year being the lowest. It gradually increased from the 11th year. In Showa 2, it temporarily decreased due to the depression of the spinning industry. It increased again in the 3rd year, reaching the highest amount. The table is as follows (unit: 1,000 yen):

Changxi on the Total Amount of Public Business in the United States Last Year 178

Among the world's great powers, the finances of the United States, which prides itself on its wealth, are worthy of our attention. According to a recent report by Schwarzchild, editor of the American Insurance Magazine, on public enterprises in 1929, there has been great progress and surpluses. The total operating revenue of public enterprises in 1928 was $562,228,200. Last year, it increased by more than $400 million compared with 1928, and the total amount was $626,290,006. This total amount is based on the reports of fifteen of the most active banking businesses in the country. First is the Hallgarten & Co., a bank that also operates enterprises. Last year, the business in enterprises was $307,065,800. The business with shared profits was $470,566,000. The second is the National City Bank's exclusive business of enterprises, which was $262,580,000. The shared profits increased almost double compared to Hallgarten & Co. In short, the increase in business and the sharp increase in surpluses of these fifteen banks, according to observations in the economic field, are all due to the development of foreign trade in the United States, and the Far East is a major reason for its sharp increase. Furthermore, last year, the total amount of statistics for various businesses in the country was $626,290,006, and the automobiles and accessories related to trade with China were $44,880,000, machinery $111,869,400, radios and accessories $29,840,500, railway materials $29,528,600, rubber $63,200,000, sports equipment and ordnance $10,075,000, cigarettes $4,143,000, industrial and factory-made sundries $96,512,000, and the turnover of kerosene reached $376,090,000. Although it cannot be entirely regarded as exploitation from China, it can be inferred that China is the largest sales market for American foreign trade.
